44018025	He had been instructed in the way of the Lord ; and being fervent in spirit , he spoke and taught accurately the things concerning Jesus , though he knew only the baptism of John .
44018026	And he began to speak out boldly in the synagogue . But when Priscilla and Aquila heard him , they took him aside and explained to him the way of God more accurately .
44018027	And when he wanted to go across to Achaia , the brethren encouraged him and wrote to the disciples to welcome him . When he had arrived , he greatly helped those who had believed through grace ,
44018028	for he powerfully refuted the Jews in public , proving by the Scriptures that Jesus was the Christ .
44019001	While Apollos was at Corinth , Paul passed through the upper country and came to Ephesus . There he found some disciples .
44019002	And he said to them , » Did you receive the Holy Spirit when you believed ? « And they said , » No , we have not even heard that there is a Holy Spirit . «
44019003	And he said , » Into what then were you baptized ? « They said , » Into John's baptism . «
44019004	Paul said , » John baptized with the baptism of repentance , telling the people to believe in the one who was coming after him , that is , in Jesus . «
44019005	On hearing this , they were baptized in the name of the Lord Jesus .
44019006	And when Paul had laid his hands upon them , the Holy Spirit came on them , and they spoke with tongues and prophesied .
44019007	There were about twelve men in all .
44019008	And he entered the synagogue and for three months spoke boldly , arguing and persuading about the kingdom of God .
44019009	But when some were stubborn and disbelieved , speaking evil of the Way before the congregation , he withdrew from them , and took the disciples with him , reasoning daily in the hall of Tyrannus .
44019010	This took place for two years , so that all who lived in the province of Asia heard the word of the Lord , both Jews and Greeks .
44019011	God did extraordinary miracles by the hands of Paul ,
44019012	so that handkerchiefs or aprons were even carried from his body to the sick , and diseases left them and the evil spirits went out .
44019013	But also some of the Jewish exorcists , who went from place to place , attempted to name over those who had the evil spirits the name of the Lord Jesus , saying , » I adjure you by Jesus whom Paul preaches . «
44019014	Seven sons of Sceva , a Jewish chief priest , were doing this .
44019015	But the evil spirit answered them , » Jesus I know , and I know about Paul , but who are you ? «
44019016	And the man in whom the evil spirit was leaped on them , overpowered all of them , and prevailed against them , so that they fled out of that house naked and wounded .
44019017	This became known to all , both Jews and Greeks , who lived in Ephesus ; and fear fell upon them all and the name of the Lord Jesus was being magnified .
44019018	Many also of those who believed now came , confessing and disclosing their practices .
44019019	And a number of those who practiced magic arts brought their books together and burned them in the sight of all ; and they counted the value of them and found it came to fifty thousand pieces of silver .
44019020	So the word of the Lord grew mightily and prevailed .
44019021	Now after these things were finished , Paul purposed in the spirit to go to Jerusalem after he had passed through Macedonia and Achaia , saying , » After I have been there , I must also see Rome . «
44019022	And having sent into Macedonia two of his helpers , Timothy and Erastus , he himself stayed in Asia for a while .
44019023	About that time there arose no small disturbance concerning the Way .
44019024	For a man named Demetrius , a silversmith , who made silver shrines of Artemis , brought no little business to the craftsmen .
44019025	These he gathered together , with the workmen of similar trades , and said , » Men , you know that from this business we have our wealth .
44019026	And you see and hear that not only in Ephesus , but in almost all of Asia , this Paul has persuaded and turned away a considerable number of people , saying that gods made with hands are no gods at all .
44019027	Not only is there danger that this trade of ours fall into disrepute , but also that the temple of the great goddess Artemis be regarded as worthless and that she whom all of Asia and the world worship will even be dethroned from her magnificence . «
44019028	When they heard this , they were enraged and began crying out , » Great is Artemis of the Ephesians ! «
44019029	The city was filled with the confusion , and they rushed with one accord into the theater , dragging along Gaius and Aristarchus , Paul's traveling companions from Macedonia .
44019030	Paul wanted to go in among the crowd , but the disciples would not let him .
44019031	Some of the Asiarchs also , who were friends of his , sent to him and begged him not to venture into the theater .
44019032	Now some were shouting one thing , some another ; for the assembly was in confusion , and most of the people did not know why they had come together .
44019033	Some of the crowd prompted Alexander , since the Jews had put him forward . And Alexander motioned with his hand , wishing to make a defense to the people .
44019034	But when they recognized that he was a Jew , for about two hours they all with one voice shouted , » Great is Artemis of the Ephesians ! «
44019035	And when the town clerk had quieted the crowd , he said , » Men of Ephesus , what man is there after all who does not know that the city of the Ephesians is guardian of the temple of the great Artemis and of the image which fell down from heaven ?
44019036	Therefore , since these facts are undeniable , you ought to be quiet and do nothing rash .
44019037	For you have brought these men here who are neither robbers of temples nor blasphemers of our goddess .
44019038	If then Demetrius and the craftsmen with him have a complaint against anyone , the courts are open , and there are proconsuls ; let them bring charges against one another .
44019039	But if you want anything further , it shall be settled in the lawful assembly .
44019040	As it is , we are in danger of being charged with rioting because of today's events . In that case we would not be able to account for this commotion , since there is no reason for it . «
44019041	After he had said this , he dismissed the assembly .
44020001	After the uproar had ceased , Paul sent for the disciples , and when he had exhorted them and taken his leave of them , he set out for Macedonia .
44020002	When he had gone through those parts and had given them much encouragement , he came to Greece .
44020003	There he spent three months , and when a plot was made against him by the Jews as he was about to set sail for Syria , he decided to return through Macedonia .
44020004	He was accompanied by Sopater of Berea , the son of Pyrrhus , and by Aristarchus and Secundus of the Thessalonians , and Gaius of Derbe , and Timothy , and Tychicus and Trophimus of Asia .
44020005	These went on ahead and were waiting for us at Troas .
44020006	But we sailed away from Philippi after the Days of Unleavened Bread , and in five days came to them at Troas , where we stayed seven days .
44020007	On the first day of the week , when we were gathered together to break bread , Paul began talking to them , intending to leave the next day , and he prolonged his message until midnight .
44020008	There were many lamps in the upper room where we were gathered .
44020009	And there was a young man named Eutychus sitting in the window sill , sinking into a deep sleep . And as Paul talked on and on , he was overcome by sleep and fell down from the third story and was picked up dead .
44020010	But Paul went down and fell on him , and after embracing him , he said , » Do not be alarmed , for his life is in him . «
44020011	When he had gone back up and had broken the bread and eaten , he talked with them a long while until daybreak , and then left .
44020012	They took away the boy alive , and were greatly comforted .
44020013	But going ahead to the ship , we set sail for Assos , intending to take Paul aboard there ; for so he had arranged , intending himself to go by land .
44020014	And when he met us at Assos , we took him on board and came to Mitylene .
44020015	Sailing from there , we arrived the following day opposite Chios ; and the next day we crossed over to Samos ; and the day after that we came to Miletus .
44020016	For Paul had decided to sail past Ephesus , so that he would not have to spend time in Asia ; for he was hurrying to be in Jerusalem , if possible , on the day of Pentecost .
44020017	From Miletus he sent to Ephesus and called to him the elders of the church .
44020018	And when they came to him , he said to them : » You yourselves know how I lived the whole time I was with you , from the first day that I set foot in Asia ,
44020019	serving the Lord with all humility and with tears and with trials which came upon me through the plots of the Jews ;
44020020	how I did not shrink from declaring to you anything that was profitable , and teaching you publicly and from house to house ,
44020021	testifying both to Jews and to Greeks of repentance toward God and faith in our Lord Jesus Christ .
44020022	And now , behold , bound in the Spirit , I am going to Jerusalem , not knowing what will happen to me there ,
44020023	except that the Holy Spirit solemnly testifies to me in every city , saying that bonds and afflictions await me .
44020024	But I do not consider my life of any account nor as precious to myself , if only I may finish my course and the ministry which I received from the Lord Jesus , to testify to the gospel of the grace of God .
44020025	And now , behold , I know that all of you among whom I have gone about preaching the kingdom will see my face no more .
44020026	Therefore , I testify to you this day that I am innocent of the blood of all men .
44020027	For I did not shrink from declaring to you the whole counsel of God .
44020028	Be on guard for yourselves and for all the flock , among which the Holy Spirit has made you overseers , to shepherd the church of God which he purchased with the blood of his Own .
44020029	I know that after my departure savage wolves will come in among you , not sparing the flock ;
44020030	and from among your own selves will arise men speaking perverse things , to draw away the disciples after them .
44020031	Therefore be alert , remembering that for three years I did not cease night and day to admonish each one with tears .
44020032	And now I commend you to God and to the word of his grace , which is able to build you up and to give you the inheritance among all those who are sanctified .
44020033	I have coveted no one's silver or gold or clothes .
44020034	You yourselves know that these hands ministered to my own needs and to the men who were with me .
44020035	In everything I did , I showed you that by this kind of hard work we must help the weak , remembering the words the Lord Jesus himself said : ‘ It is more blessed to give than to receive . ’ «
44020036	When he had said this , he knelt down and prayed with them all .
44020037	And they all wept and embraced Paul and kissed him ,
44020038	grieving most of all over the word which he had spoken , that they would not see his face again . And they accompanied him to the ship .
44021001	When we had parted from them and set sail , we came by a straight course to Cos , and the next day to Rhodes , and from there to Patara .
44021002	And having found a ship crossing over to Phoenicia , we went aboard and set sail .
44021003	When we had come in sight of Cyprus , leaving it on the left we sailed to Syria , and landed at Tyre ; for there the ship was to unload its cargo .
44021004	And having sought out the disciples , we stayed there for seven days . Through the Spirit they told Paul not to go on to Jerusalem .
44021005	And when our days there were ended , we left and started on our journey , while they all , with wives and children , brought us on our way until we were out of the city . After kneeling down on the beach and praying , we said farewell to one another .
44021006	Then we went on board the ship , and they returned home .
44021007	When we had finished the voyage from Tyre , we arrived at Ptolemais ; and we greeted the brethren and stayed with them for a day .
44021008	On the next day we left and came to Caesarea , and entering the house of Philip the evangelist , who was one of the seven , we stayed with him .
44021009	He had four unmarried daughters who prophesied .
44021010	As we were staying there for some days , a prophet named Agabus came down from Judea .
44021011	And coming to us , he took Paul's belt and bound his own feet and hands , and said , » This is what the Holy Spirit says , ‘ In this way the Jews at Jerusalem will bind the man who owns this belt and deliver him into the hands of the Gentiles . ’ «
44021012	When we heard this , we and the people there begged him not to go up to Jerusalem .
44021013	Then Paul answered , » What are you doing , weeping and breaking my heart ? For I am ready not only to be bound but even to die at Jerusalem for the name of the Lord Jesus . «
44021014	And when he would not be persuaded , we ceased and said , » The will of the Lord be done . «
44021015	After these days we got ready and went up to Jerusalem .
44021016	And some of the disciples from Caesarea went with us , bringing us to the house of Mnason of Cyprus , an early disciple , with whom we were to lodge .
44021017	When we arrived at Jerusalem , the brethren received us gladly .
44021018	And the following day Paul went in with us to James , and all the elders were present .
44021019	After he had greeted them , he related one by one the things that God had done among the Gentiles through his ministry .
44021020	And when they heard it , they glorified God . And they said to him , » You see , brother , how many thousands there are among the Jews of those who have believed ; they are all zealous for the law ,
44021021	and they have been told about you that you teach all the Jews who are among the Gentiles to forsake Moses , telling them not to circumcise their children or to walk according to the customs .
44021022	What then is to be done ? They will certainly hear that you have come .
44021023	Therefore do what we tell you . We have four men who are under a vow ;
44021024	take these men and purify yourself along with them and pay their expenses , so that they may shave their heads . Thus all will know that there is nothing in what they have been told about you , but that you yourself live in observance of the law .
44021025	But as for the Gentiles who have believed , we wrote to them our decision that they should abstain from meat sacrificed to idols and from blood and from what is strangled and from fornication . «
44021026	The next day Paul took the men and purified himself along with them . Then he went to the temple to give notice of the date when the days of purification would end and the offering would be made for each one of them .
44021027	When the seven days were almost over , the Jews from Asia , upon seeing him in the temple , stirred up all the crowd and laid hands on him ,
44021028	crying out , » Men of Israel , help ! This is the man who is teaching all men everywhere against our people and our law and this place ; and besides he also brought Greeks into the temple , and he has defiled this holy place . «
44021029	For they had previously seen Trophimus the Ephesian in the city with him , and they supposed that Paul had brought him into the temple .
44021030	Then all the city was aroused , and the people rushed together , and taking hold of Paul they dragged him out of the temple , and immediately the gates were shut .
44021031	While they were trying to kill him , a report came up to the commander of the Roman cohort that all Jerusalem was in confusion .
44021032	At once he took along some soldiers and centurions and ran down to them ; and when they saw the commander and the soldiers , they stopped beating Paul .
44021033	Then the commander came up and arrested him , and ordered him to be bound with two chains . He inquired who he was and what he had done .
44021034	Some in the crowd shouted one thing , and some another ; and as he could not learn the facts because of the uproar , he ordered him to be brought into the barracks .
44021035	When he came to the steps , he was actually carried by the soldiers because of the violence of the mob ;
44021036	for the mob of the people followed , shouting , » Away with him ! «
44021037	As Paul was about to be brought into the barracks , he said to the commander , » May I say something to you ? « And he said , » Do you know Greek ?
44021038	Then you are not the Egyptian who some time ago stirred up a revolt and led the four thousand men of the Assassins out into the wilderness ? «
44021039	Paul replied , » I am a Jew , from Tarsus in Cilicia , a citizen of no insignificant city ; I beg you , let me speak to the people . «
44021040	When he had given him permission , Paul , standing on the steps , motioned to the people with his hand ; and when there was a great hush , he spoke to them in the Hebrew language , saying ,
44022001	» Brethren and fathers , hear my defense which I now offer to you . «
44022002	And when they heard that he addressed them in the Hebrew language , they became more quiet . And he said :
44022003	» I am a Jew , born in Tarsus of Cilicia , but brought up in this city , educated under Gamaliel , strictly according to the law of our fathers , being zealous for God just as you all are today .
44022004	I persecuted this Way to the death , binding and delivering into prison both men and women ,
44022005	as also the high priest and all the Council of the elders can testify . From them I also received letters to the brethren , and started off for Damascus in order to bring even those who were there to Jerusalem as prisoners to be punished .
44022006	» As I made my journey and drew near to Damascus , about noon a bright light from heaven suddenly flashed around me .
44022007	And I fell to the ground and heard a voice saying to me , ‘ Saul , Saul , why do you persecute me ? ’
44022008	And I answered , ‘ Who are you , Lord ? ’ And he said to me , ‘ I am Jesus of Nazareth , whom you are persecuting . ’
44022009	And those who were with me saw the light , but did not hear the voice of the one who was speaking to me .
44022010	And I said , ‘ What shall I do , Lord ? ’ And the Lord said to me , ‘ Get up and go on into Damascus , and there you will be told of all that has been appointed for you to do . ’
44022011	But since I could not see because of the brightness of that light , I was led by the hand by those who were with me and came into Damascus .
44022012	» A certain Ananias , a devout man according to the Law , and well spoken of by all the Jews who lived there ,
44022013	came to me , and standing near said to me , ‘ Brother Saul , receive your sight ! ’ And at that very time I looked up at him .
44022014	Then he said , ‘ The God of our fathers has appointed you to know his will and to see the Righteous One and to hear words from his mouth .
44022015	For you will be a witness for him to all men of what you have seen and heard .
44022016	Now why do you delay ? Get up and be baptized , and wash away your sins , calling on his name . ’
44022017	» When I had returned to Jerusalem and was praying in the temple , I fell into a trance
44022018	and saw him saying to me , ‘ Make haste , and get out of Jerusalem quickly , because they will not accept your testimony about me . ’
44022019	And I said , ‘ Lord , they themselves know that in one synagogue after another I used to imprison and beat those who believed in you .
44022020	When the blood of Stephen your witness was shed , I also was standing by and approving , and keeping the garments of those who were killing him . ’
44022021	And he said to me , ‘ Go ; for I will send you far away to the Gentiles . ’ «
44022022	Up to this word they listened to him , and then they raised their voices and said , » Away with such a fellow from the earth ! For he ought not to live . «
44022023	And as they were crying out and throwing off their cloaks and tossing dust into the air ,
44022024	the commander ordered him to be brought into the barracks , and commanded him to be examined by scourging so that he might find out the reason why they were shouting against him that way .
44022025	But when they stretched him out with thongs , Paul said to the centurion who was standing by , » Is it lawful for you to scourge a man who is a Roman citizen and uncondemned ? «
44022026	When the centurion heard this , he went to the commander and told him , saying , » What are you about to do ? For this man is a Roman citizen . «
44022027	So the commander came and said to him , » Tell me , are you a Roman citizen ? « And he said , » Yes . «
44022028	The commander answered , » I bought this citizenship for a large sum . « Paul said , » But I was born a citizen . «
44022029	So those who were about to examine him withdrew from him immediately ; and the commander also was afraid when he realized that Paul was a Roman citizen and that he had put him in chains .
44022030	But on the next day , wishing to know for certain why he had been accused by the Jews , he released him and ordered the chief priests and all the Council to assemble , and brought Paul down and set him before them .
44023001	And Paul , looking intently at the council , said , » Brethren , I have lived my life before God in all good conscience up to this day . «
44023002	The high priest Ananias commanded those standing beside him to strike him on the mouth .
44023003	Then Paul said to him , » God shall strike you , you whitewashed wall ! Do you sit to judge me according to the law , and yet contrary to the law you order me to be struck ? «
44023004	Those who stood by said , » Would you revile God's high priest ? «
44023005	And Paul said , » I did not know , brethren , that he was the high priest ; for it is written , ‘ You shall not speak evil of a ruler of your people . ’ «
44023006	But when Paul perceived that one part were Sadducees and the other Pharisees , he cried out in the council , » Brethren , I am a Pharisee , a son of Pharisees ; with respect to the hope and the resurrection of the dead I am on trial . «
44023007	When he said this , a dissension broke out between the Pharisees and the Sadducees , and the assembly was divided .
44023008	For the Sadducees say that there is no resurrection , nor an angel , nor a spirit , but the Pharisees acknowledge them all .
44023009	There occurred a great uproar ; and some of the scribes of the Pharisees' party stood up and began to argue heatedly , saying , » We find nothing wrong with this man . What if a spirit or an angel has spoken to him ? «
44023010	The dispute became so violent that the commander was afraid Paul would be torn to pieces by them and ordered the troops to go down and take him away from them by force , and bring him into the barracks .
44023011	The following night the Lord stood by him and said , » Take courage , for as you have testified about me at Jerusalem , so you must bear witness also at Rome . «
44023012	When it was day , the Jews formed a conspiracy and bound themselves by an oath neither to eat nor drink until they had killed Paul .
44023013	There were more than forty who formed this plot .
44023014	They went to the chief priests and the elders and said , » We have bound ourselves under a solemn oath to taste nothing until we have killed Paul .
44023015	You therefore , along with the council , give notice now to the commander to bring him down to you , as though you were going to determine his case more exactly . And we are ready to kill him before he comes near . «
44023016	But the son of Paul's sister heard of their ambush , and he went and entered the barracks and told Paul .
44023017	Paul called one of the centurions and said , » Take this young man to the commander ; for he has something to tell him . «
44023018	So he took him and brought him to the commander and said , » Paul the prisoner called me and asked me to bring this young man to you , since he has something to tell you . «
44023019	The commander took him by the hand , and going aside asked him privately , » What is it that you have to tell me ? «
44023020	And he said , » The Jews have agreed to ask you to bring Paul down tomorrow to the Council , as though they were going to inquire somewhat more thoroughly about him .
44023021	But do not yield to them ; for more than forty of them are waiting in ambush for him , having bound themselves by an oath neither to eat nor drink until they have killed him ; and now they are ready , waiting for the promise from you . «
44023022	So the commander dismissed the young man , instructing him , » Tell no one that you have informed me of this . «
44023023	Then he called two of the centurions and said , » At the third hour of the night get ready two hundred soldiers with seventy horsemen and two hundred spearmen to go as far as Caesarea .
44023024	Also provide mounts for Paul to ride , and bring him safely to Felix the governor . «
44023025	And he wrote a letter having this form :
44023026	» Claudius Lysias , to His Excellency , Governor Felix : greetings .
44023027	This man was seized by the Jews , and was about to be killed by them , when I came upon them with the troops and rescued him , having learned that he was a Roman citizen .
44023028	And desiring to know the charge for which they were accusing him , I brought him down to their council .
44023029	I found that he was accused over questions about their Law , but there was no accusation against him deserving death or imprisonment .
44023030	And when I was informed that there would be a plot against the man , I sent him to you at once , also instructing his accusers to bring charges against him before you . «
44023031	So the soldiers , in accordance with their orders , took Paul and brought him by night to Antipatris .
44023032	But the next day , leaving the horsemen to go on with him , they returned to the barracks .
44023033	When these had come to Caesarea and delivered the letter to the governor , they also presented Paul to him .
44023034	When he had read the letter , he asked from what province he was , and when he learned that he was from Cilicia ,
44023035	he said , » I will hear you when your accusers arrive also . « And he commanded him to be kept in Herod's Praetorium .
44024001	After five days the high priest Ananias came down with some elders , with an attorney named Tertullus , and they brought their charges against Paul before the governor .
44024002	And when Paul was called , Tertullus began to accuse him , saying to Felix : » Since through you we have enjoyed much peace , and since by your provision , reforms are introduced on behalf of this nation ,
44024003	we acknowledge this in every way and everywhere , most excellent Felix , with all gratitude .
44024004	But , that I may not weary you further , I beg you in your kindness to hear us briefly .
44024005	For we have found this man a pestilent fellow who stirs up dissension among all the Jews throughout the world , and a ringleader of the sect of the Nazarenes .
44024006	He even tried to desecrate the temple ; so we seized him .
44024008	By examining him yourself you will be able to learn the truth about all these charges of which we accuse him . «
44024009	The Jews also joined in the attack , asserting that these things were so .
44024010	When the governor had motioned for him to speak , Paul replied : » Realizing that for many years you have been a judge over this nation , I cheerfully make my defense .
44024011	Since you can easily verify that no more than twelve days ago I went up to Jerusalem to worship .
44024012	They did not find me disputing with anyone or stirring up a crowd , either in the temple or in the synagogues , or in the city .
44024013	Neither can they prove to you the charges they are now making against me .
44024014	But this I admit to you , that according to the Way which they call a sect I do worship the God of our fathers , believing everything that is in accordance with the Law and that is written in the Prophets ,
44024015	having a hope in God , which these men cherish themselves , that there will certainly be a resurrection of both the righteous and the wicked .
44024016	And so I do my best always to have a clear conscience before God and men .
44024017	Now after several years I came to bring alms to my nation and to present offerings .
44024018	As I was doing this , they found me purified in the temple , without any crowd or uproar . But there were some Jews from Asia —
44024019	who ought to be here before you and to make accusation , if they should have anything against me .
44024020	Or else let these men themselves tell what wrongdoing they found when I stood before the Council ,
44024021	except this one thing which I shouted out while standing among them , ‘ With respect to the resurrection of the dead I am on trial before you today . ’ «
44024022	But Felix , having a more exact knowledge about the Way , put them off , saying , » When Lysias the commander comes down , I will decide your case . «
44024023	Then he gave orders to the centurion for him to be kept in custody but have some freedom , and not to prevent any of his friends from ministering to his needs .
44024024	But some days later Felix came with Drusilla , his wife who was a Jewess , and sent for Paul and heard him speak about faith in Christ Jesus .
44024025	But as he was discussing righteousness , self-control and the judgment to come , Felix became frightened and said , » Go away for the present , and when I find time I will summon you . «
44024026	At the same time , he was hoping that money would be given him by Paul . So he sent for him often and conversed with him .
44024027	But when two years had passed , Felix was succeeded by Porcius Festus , and desiring to do the Jews a favor , Felix left Paul in prison .
44025001	Festus then , three days after arriving in the province , went up to Jerusalem from Caesarea .
44025002	And the chief priests and the principal men of the Jews brought charges against Paul ; and they urged him ,
44025003	as a favor to them , to have Paul transferred to Jerusalem , for they were preparing an ambush to kill him along the way .
44025004	Festus answered that Paul was being kept at Caesarea , and that he himself intended to go there shortly .
44025005	» Therefore , « he said , » let the men of authority among you go there with me , and if there is anything wrong about the man , let them prosecute him . «
44025006	After he had spent not more than eight or ten days among them , he went down to Caesarea , and on the next day he took his seat on the tribunal and ordered Paul to be brought .
44025007	And when Paul arrived , the Jews who had come down from Jerusalem stood around him , bringing many serious charges against him , which they could not prove .
44025008	Paul said in his defense , » Neither against the law of the Jews , nor against the temple , nor against Caesar have I offended at all . «
44025009	But Festus , wishing to do the Jews a favor , said to Paul , » Are you willing to go up to Jerusalem and stand trial before me there on these charges ? «
44025010	But Paul said , » I am standing before Caesar's tribunal , where I ought to be tried . I have done no wrong to the Jews , as you also very well know .
44025011	If , then , I am a wrongdoer and have committed anything worthy of death , I do not refuse to die ; but if none of the charges brought against me is true , no one can hand me over to them . I appeal to Caesar . «
44025012	Then when Festus had conferred with his council , he answered , » You have appealed to Caesar , to Caesar you shall go . «
44025013	Now when a few days had passed , King Agrippa and Bernice arrived at Caesarea and paid their respects to Festus .
44025014	While they were spending many days there , Festus laid Paul's case before the king , saying , » There is a man who was left as a prisoner by Felix ;
44025015	and when I was at Jerusalem , the chief priests and the elders of the Jews brought charges against him , asking for sentence against him .
44025016	I answered them that it is not the custom of the Romans to hand over any man before the accused meets his accusers face to face and has an opportunity to make his defense against the charges .
44025017	When therefore they came together here , I did not delay , but on the next day took my seat on the tribunal and ordered the man to be brought in .
44025018	When the accusers stood up , they did not charge him of such crimes as I had expected ,
44025019	but they simply had some points of dispute with him about their own religion and about a dead man , Jesus , whom Paul asserted to be alive .
44025020	Being at a loss how to investigate such matters , I asked whether he was willing to go to Jerusalem and there stand trial on these matters .
44025021	But when Paul appealed to be held in custody for the Emperor's decision , I ordered him to be kept in custody until I could send him to Caesar .
44025022	Then Agrippa said to Festus , » I also would like to hear the man myself . « » Tomorrow , « he said , » you shall hear him . «
44025023	So on the next day Agrippa and Bernice came with great pomp and entered the audience room with the high ranking officers and the prominent men of the city . At the command of Festus , Paul was brought in .
44025024	Festus said , » King Agrippa and all who are present with us , you see this man about whom the whole Jewish people petitioned me , both at Jerusalem and here , shouting that he ought not to live any longer .
44025025	But I found that he had done nothing deserving of death ; and as he himself appealed to the emperor , I decided to send him .
44025026	But I have nothing definite about him to write to my lord . Therefore I have brought him before you all and especially before you , King Agrippa , so that after the investigation has taken place , I may have something to write .
44025027	For it seems to me unreasonable , in sending a prisoner , not to indicate the charges against him . «
44026001	Agrippa said to Paul , » You have permission to speak for yourself . « Then Paul stretched out his hand and began his defense :
44026002	» I consider myself fortunate that it is before you , King Agrippa , I am to make my defense today against all the accusations of the Jews ,
44026003	because you are especially familiar with all customs and controversies of the Jews ; therefore I beg you to listen to me patiently .
44026004	So then , all the Jews know my manner of life from my youth up , which from the beginning was spent among my own nation and at Jerusalem .
44026005	They have known about me for a long time , if they are willing to testify , that I lived as a Pharisee according to the strictest sect of our religion .
44026006	And now I am standing trial for the hope of the promise made by God to our fathers ;
44026007	the promise to which our twelve tribes hope to attain , as they earnestly serve God night and day . And for this hope , O King , I am being accused by Jews .
44026008	Why is it thought incredible by any of you that God raises the dead ?
44026009	I myself was convinced that I ought to do many things to oppose the name of Jesus of Nazareth .
44026010	And that is just what I did in Jerusalem ; I not only shut up many of the saints in prison , by authority from the chief priests , but when they were put to death I cast my vote against them .
44026011	And as I punished them often in all the synagogues , I tried to force them to blaspheme ; and being furiously enraged against them , I persecuted them even to foreign cities .
44026012	» On one of these journeys I was going to Damascus with the authority and commission of the chief priests .
44026013	At midday , O King , I saw on the way a light from heaven , brighter than the sun , shining around me and those who journeyed with me .
44026014	And when we had all fallen to the ground , I heard a voice saying to me in the Hebrew language , ‘ Saul , Saul , why do you persecute me ? It is hard for you to kick against the goads . ’
44026015	And I said , ‘ Who are you , Lord ? ’ And the Lord said , ‘ I am Jesus whom you are persecuting .
44026016	But get up and stand on your feet ; for this purpose I have appeared to you , to appoint you a minister and a witness to the things which you have seen of me , and also to the things in which I will appear to you ;
44026017	rescuing you from the Jewish people and from the Gentiles , to whom I am sending you ,
44026018	to open their eyes , so that they may turn from darkness to light and from the power of Satan to God , that they may receive forgiveness of sins and a place among those who are sanctified by faith in me . ’
44026019	» So , King Agrippa , I was not disobedient to the heavenly vision ,
44026020	but declared first to those at Damascus , then at Jerusalem and throughout all the country of Judea , and also to the Gentiles , that they should repent and turn to God and perform deeds worthy of their repentance .
44026021	For this reason the Jews seized me in the temple and tried to kill me .
44026022	To this day I have had the help that comes from God , and so I stand here testifying both to small and great , saying nothing but what the prophets and Moses said would happen :
44026023	that the Christ must suffer , and that , by being the first to rise from the dead , he would proclaim light both to the people and to the Gentiles . «
44026024	And as he was saying this in his defense , Festus said in a loud voice , » Paul , you are out of your mind ! Your great learning is driving you mad . «
44026025	But Paul said , » I am not mad , most excellent Festus , but I am speaking the sober truth .
44026026	For the king knows about these things , and to him I speak freely ; for I am persuaded that none of these things has escaped his notice , for this was not done in a corner .
44026027	King Agrippa , do you believe the prophets ? I know that you do . «
44026028	And Agrippa said to Paul , » In a short time you think to persuade me to become a Christian ! «
44026029	And Paul said , » Whether in a short or a long time , I would to God that not only you but also all who hear me this day might become such as I am — except for these chains . «
44026030	The king rose and the governor and Bernice , and those who were sitting with them ,
44026031	and when they had gone aside , they began talking to one another , saying , » This man is not doing anything worthy of death or imprisonment . «
44026032	And Agrippa said to Festus , » This man could have been set free if he had not appealed to Caesar . «
44027001	When it was decided that we would sail for Italy , they delivered Paul and some other prisoners to a centurion of the Augustan cohort named Julius .
44027002	And embarking in a ship from Adramyttium , which was about to sail to the ports along the coast of Asia , we put out to sea , accompanied by Aristarchus , a Macedonian from Thessalonica .
44027003	The next day we put in at Sidon ; and Julius treated Paul kindly , and allowed him to go to his friends and be cared for .
44027004	We put out to sea from there and sailed under the lee of Cyprus , because the winds were against us .
44027005	When we had sailed across the open sea off the coast of Cilicia and Pamphylia , we landed at Myra in Lycia .
44027006	There the centurion found an Alexandrian ship sailing for Italy , and he put us aboard it .
44027007	When we had sailed slowly for a good many days , and with difficulty had arrived off Cnidus , since the wind did not allow us to go farther , we sailed under the lee of Crete , off Salmone .
44027008	We sailed along it with difficulty and came to a place called Fair Havens , near which was the city of Lasea .
44027009	As much time had been lost , and the voyage was now dangerous because the fast had already gone by , Paul advised them ,
44027010	and said to them , » Men , I perceive that the voyage will be with injury and great loss , not only of the cargo and the ship , but also of our lives . «
44027011	But the centurion was more persuaded by the pilot and the owner of the ship than by what was being said by Paul .
44027012	Because the harbor was not suitable to winter in , the majority reached a decision to put out to sea from there , on the chance that somehow they could reach Phoenix , a harbor of Crete , facing southwest and northwest , and spend the winter there .
44027013	When a gentle south wind came up , supposing that they had obtained their purpose , they weighed anchor and began sailing along Crete , close inshore .
44027014	But before very long there rushed down from the land a violent wind , called the northeaster ;
44027015	and when the ship was caught in it and could not face the wind , we gave way to it and were driven along .
44027016	And running under the lee of a small island called Cauda , we were scarcely able to secure the boat .
44027017	After they had hoisted it up , they used supporting cables to undergird the ship ; and fearing that they might run aground on the shallows of Syrtis , they lowered the sea anchor and in this way let themselves be driven along .
44027018	The next day as we were being violently storm-tossed , they began to throw the cargo overboard ;
44027019	and on the third day they threw the ship's tackle overboard with their own hands .
44027020	When neither sun nor stars appeared for many days , and no small storm was raging on us , all hope of our being saved was finally abandoned .
44027021	When they had gone a long time without food , then Paul stood up among them and said , » Men , you should have followed my advice and not to have set sail from Crete and incurred this damage and loss .
44027022	Yet now I urge you to keep up your courage ; for there will be no loss of life among you , but only of the ship .
44027023	For this very night an angel of the God to whom I belong and whom I serve stood before me ,
44027024	and he said , ‘ Do not be afraid , Paul ; you must stand before Caesar ; and behold , God has granted you all those who sail with you . ’
44027025	So keep up your courage , men , for I have faith in God that it will happen exactly as I have been told .
44027026	But we must run aground on some island . «
44027027	But when the fourteenth night came , as we were being driven across the Adriatic Sea , about midnight the sailors began to sense that they were approaching land .
44027028	They took soundings and found it to be twenty fathoms ; and a little farther on they took soundings again and found it to be fifteen fathoms .
44027029	Fearing that we might run aground somewhere on the rocks , they cast four anchors from the stern and prayed for daybreak .
44027030	But as the sailors were trying to escape from the ship and had let down the lifeboat into the sea , on the pretense of laying out anchors from the bow ,
44027031	Paul said to the centurion and the soldiers , » Unless these men stay in the ship , you cannot be saved . «
44027032	Then the soldiers cut the ropes of the lifeboat and let it fall away .
44027033	As day was about to dawn , Paul urged them all to take some food , saying , » Today is the fourteenth day that you have been in suspense and without food , having taken nothing .
44027034	Therefore I urge you to take some food ; it will give you strength , since not a hair is to perish from the head of any of you . «
44027035	Having said this , he took bread and gave thanks to God in the presence of all , and he broke it and began to eat .
44027036	Then they all were encouraged and ate some food themselves .
44027037	All of us in the ship were two hundred and seventy-six persons .
44027038	When they had eaten enough , they lightened the ship by throwing out the wheat into the sea .
44027039	When day came , they could not recognize the land , but they did observe a bay with a beach , and they resolved to drive the ship onto it if they could .
44027040	So they cast off the anchors and left them in the sea , at the same time loosening the ropes that tied the rudders ; then hoisting the foresail to the wind they made for the beach .
44027041	But striking a sandbar they ran the vessel aground ; the bow stuck fast and remained immovable , and the stern was broken up by the pounding of the surf .
44027042	The soldiers' plan was to kill the prisoners , so that none of them would swim away and escape .
44027043	But the centurion , wanting to bring Paul safely through , kept them from carrying out their plan . He ordered those who could swim to jump overboard first and get to land ,
44027044	and the rest on planks or on various pieces of the ship . And so it happened that they were all brought safely to land .
44028001	When we had been brought safely through , then we found out that the island was called Malta .
44028002	The natives showed us unusual kindness , for they kindled a fire and welcomed us all , because it had begun to rain and was cold .
44028003	But when Paul had gathered a bundle of sticks and put them on the fire , a viper came out because of the heat and fastened itself on his hand .
44028004	When the natives saw the creature hanging from his hand , they said to one another , » No doubt this man is a murderer . Though he has escaped from the sea , justice has not allowed him to live . «
44028005	However he shook the creature off into the fire and suffered no harm .
44028006	They waited , expecting him to swell up or suddenly fall down dead ; but after they had waited a long time and saw nothing unusual happen to him , they changed their minds and said that he was a god .
44028007	Now in the neighborhood of that place were lands belonging to the chief man of the island , named Publius , who welcomed us and entertained us hospitably for three days .
44028008	It happened that the father of Publius was lying in bed sick with recurrent fever and dysentery ; and Paul went in to see him and after he had prayed , he laid his hands on him and healed him .
44028009	When this had happened , the rest of the people on the island who had diseases also came and were cured .
44028010	They honored us in many ways ; and when we were ready to sail , they furnished us with the supplies we needed .
44028011	After three months we set sail in a ship which had wintered in the island , an Alexandrian ship , with the Twin Brothers as figurehead .
44028012	After we put in at Syracuse , we stayed there for three days .
44028013	From there we sailed around and arrived at Rhegium , and a day later a south wind sprang up , and on the second day we came to Puteoli .
44028014	There we found some brethren , and were invited to stay with them for seven days . And so we came to Rome .
44028015	And the brethren , when they heard of us , came from there as far as the Forum of Appius and Three Taverns to meet us . When Paul saw them , he thanked God and took courage .
44028016	And when we came into Rome , Paul was allowed to stay by himself , with the soldier that guarded him .
44028017	After three days Paul called together the local leaders of the Jews ; and when they had gathered , he said to them , » Brethren , though I had done nothing against our people or the customs of our fathers , yet I was delivered prisoner from Jerusalem into the hands of the Romans .
44028018	And when they had examined me , they were willing to release me because there was no ground for putting me to death .
44028019	But when the Jews objected , I was compelled to appeal to Caesar — not that I had any charge to bring against my own nation .
44028020	For this reason therefore I have asked to see you and speak with you , since it is because of the hope of Israel that I am bound with this chain . «
44028021	They said to him , » We have not received letters from Judea concerning you , and none of the brethren who have come here has reported or spoken anything bad about you .
44028022	But we desire to hear from you what your views are ; for concerning this sect , we know that everywhere it is spoken against . «
44028023	When they had appointed a day for Paul , they came to him at his lodging in great numbers . And he explained the matter to them from morning till evening , testifying to the kingdom of God and trying to convince them about Jesus both from the law of Moses and from the prophets .
44028024	Some were convinced by what he said , but others would not believe .
44028025	When they disagreed among themselves , they began to leave , after Paul had made one final statement : » The Holy Spirit spoke the truth to your fathers through Isaiah the prophet :
44028026	saying , ‘ Go to this people and say , » you will be ever hearing , but will never understand ; and you will be ever seeing , but will never perceive .
44028027	
44028028	Therefore let it be known to you that this salvation of God has been sent to the Gentiles ; they will listen . «
44028030	And he stayed there two whole years in his own rented quarters and welcomed all who came to him ,
44028031	preaching the kingdom of God and teaching about the Lord Jesus Christ quite openly and unhindered .
45001001	Paul , a servant of Jesus Christ , called to be an apostle , set apart for the gospel of God
45001002	which he promised beforehand through his prophets in the Holy Scriptures ,
45001003	concerning his Son , who was born of the seed of David according to the flesh ,
45001004	and declared to be the Son of God with power according to the Spirit of holiness by his resurrection from the dead , Jesus Christ our Lord .
45001005	Through him we have received grace and apostleship to bring about the obedience of faith for the sake of his name among all the nations ,
45001006	among whom you also are called to belong to Jesus Christ ;
45001007	To all in Rome who are beloved of God , called to be saints : Grace to you and peace from God our Father and the Lord Jesus Christ .
45001008	First , I thank my God through Jesus Christ for all of you , because your faith is proclaimed in all the world .
45001009	For God is my witness , whom I serve with my spirit in the gospel of his Son , that without ceasing I mention you always in my prayers ,
45001010	asking that somehow by God's will I may now at last find the way to come to you .
45001011	For I long to see you , so that I may impart to you some spiritual gift to strengthen you —
45001012	that is , that you and I may be mutually encouraged by each other's faith .
45001013	I do not want you to be unaware , brethren , that I often planned to come to you ( but have been prevented from doing so until now ) in order that I might have some harvest among you , just as I have had among the other Gentiles .
45001014	I am under obligation both to Greeks and to barbarians , both to the wise and to the foolish :
45001015	so I am eager to preach the gospel to you also who are in Rome .
45001016	For I am not ashamed of the gospel : for it is the power of God for the salvation of everyone who believes , to the Jew first and also to the Greek .
45001017	For in it the righteousness of God is revealed from faith to faith ; as it is written , » The just shall live by faith . «
45001018	For the wrath of God is revealed from heaven against all ungodliness and wickedness of men who by their wickedness suppress the truth ,
45001019	for what may be known about God is plain to them , because God has shown it to them .
45001020	For since the creation of the world his invisible nature , even his eternal power and deity , has been clearly seen , being understood by the things that have been made . So they are without excuse ;
45001021	for although they knew God they did not honor him as God or give thanks to him , but they became futile in their thinking , and their foolish hearts were darkened .
45001022	Claiming to be wise , they became fools ,
45001023	and exchanged the glory of the immortal God for images made like mortal man and birds and animals and reptiles .
45001024	Therefore God gave them up in the lusts of their hearts to impurity , to the dishonoring of their bodies among themselves ,
45001025	because they exchanged the truth of God for a lie and worshipped and served the creature rather than the Creator , who is blessed forever . Amen .
45001026	For this reason God gave them up to dishonorable passions . Even their women exchanged natural relations for unnatural .
45001027	And the men likewise gave up natural relations with women and were consumed with passion for one another , men committing shameless acts with men and receiving in their own persons the due penalty for their error .
45001028	And since they did not see fit to retain the knowledge of God , God gave them over to a base mind , to do what ought not to be done .
45001029	They were filled with all manner of wickedness , evil , covetousness , depravity . Full of envy , murder , strife , deceit , malice ; they are gossips ,
45001030	slanderers , haters of God , insolent , arrogant , boastful , inventors of evil , disobedient to parents ,
45001031	foolish , faithless , heartless , ruthless .
45001032	Though they know God's righteous decree that those who do such things deserve death , they not only continue to do these very things but also approve of those who practice them .
45002001	Therefore you have no excuse , O man , whoever you are who judge another ; for in whatever point you pass judgment on him you condemn yourself , because you , the judge , are doing the very same things .
45002002	We know that the judgment of God is according to truth against those who do such things .
45002003	Do you think , O man , that when you judge those who do such things and yet do the same yourself , you will escape the judgment of God ?
45002004	Or do you presume upon the riches of his kindness and forbearance and patience ? Do you not know that God's kindness is meant to lead you to repentance ?
45002005	But by your hardness and your impenitent heart you are storing up wrath for yourself on the day of wrath when God's righteous judgment will be revealed .
45002006	For he » will render to each one according to his works « :
45002007	to those who by patience in doing good seek for glory , honor , and immortality , he will give eternal life ;
45002008	but for those who are self-seeking and do not obey the truth , but obey wickedness , there will be wrath and fury .
45002009	There will be tribulation and distress for every human being who does evil , the Jew first and also the Greek ,
45002010	but glory , honor , and peace for everyone who does good , the Jew first and also the Greek .
45002011	For God shows no partiality .
45002012	All who have sinned without the law will also perish without the law , and all who have sinned under the law will be judged by the law .
45002013	For it is not the hearers of the law who are righteous in the sight of God , but the doers of the law who will be justified .
45002014	When Gentiles , who have not the law , do by nature things required by the law , they are a law to themselves , even though they do not have the law .
45002015	They show that the requirements of the law are written on their hearts , their conscience also bearing witness , and their thoughts accusing or else excusing them
45002016	on that day when , according to my gospel , God will judge the secrets of men by Christ Jesus .
45002017	But if you call yourself a Jew , and rely on the law and boast of your relation to God
45002018	and know his will and approve of what is excellent , because you are instructed in the law ,
45002019	and if you are sure that you are a guide to the blind , a light to those who are in darkness ,
45002020	an instructor of the foolish , a teacher of infants , having in the law the embodiment of knowledge and truth —
45002021	you , then , who teach others , do you not teach yourself ? You who preach against stealing , do you steal ?
45002022	You who say that one must not commit adultery , do you commit adultery ? You who abhor idols , do you rob temples ?
45002023	You who boast in the law , do you dishonor God by breaking the law ?
45002024	For , as it is written , » The name of God is blasphemed among the Gentiles because of you . «
45002025	Circumcision indeed is of value if you obey the law ; but if you break the law , your circumcision has become uncircumcision .
45002026	So , if a man who is uncircumcised keeps the requirements of the law , will not his uncircumcision be regarded as circumcision ?
45002027	The one who is not circumcised physically and yet obeys the law will condemn you who , even though you have the written code and circumcision , are a breaker of the law .
45002028	For he is not a real Jew who is one outwardly , nor is true circumcision something outward and in the flesh .
45002029	He is a Jew who is one inwardly ; and real circumcision is a matter of the heart , by the Spirit , and not by the written code . His praise is not from men but from God .
45003001	Then what advantage has the Jew , or what is the value of circumcision ?
45003002	Much in every way ! To begin with , they are entrusted with the oracles of God .
45003003	What if some did not have faith ? Will their faithlessness nullify the faithfulness of God ?
45003004	Certainly not ! Let God be true , though every man a liar . As it is written : » That you may be justified in your words and prevail when you are judged . «
45003005	But if our unrighteousness serves to show the righteousness of God , what shall we say ? That God is unjust to inflict wrath on us ? ( I speak in a human way . )
45003006	Certainly not ! For then how could God judge the world ?
45003007	But if through my falsehood God's truthfulness abounds to his glory , why am I still being condemned as a sinner ?
45003008	Why not say – as we are being slanderously reported as saying and as some claim that we say — » Let us do evil that good may come « ? Their condemnation is just .
45003009	What then ? Are we Jews any better off ? Certainly not ; for we have already charged that all men , both Jews and Greeks , are under the power of sin .
45003010	As it is written : » There is none righteous , no , not one ;
45003011	
45003012	
45003013	
45003014	
45003015	
45003016	
45003017	
45003018	
45003019	Now we know that whatever the law says , it says to those who are under the law , so that every mouth may be stopped and the whole world may be held accountable to God .
45003020	Therefore no flesh will be justified in his sight by works of the law , for through the law comes knowledge of sin .
45003021	But now the righteousness of God has been revealed apart from law , although the law and the prophets bear witness to it ,
45003022	the righteousness of God through faith in Jesus Christ to all who believe . For there is no difference ,
45003023	for all have sinned and fall short of the glory of God ,
45003024	and are justified freely by his grace through the redemption that is in Christ Jesus ,
45003025	whom God put forward as an atoning sacrifice by his blood , to be received through faith . This was to demonstrate his righteousness , because in his divine forbearance he had passed over sins committed beforehand ;
45003026	and it was to demonstrate his righteousness at the present time , that he might be just and the justifier of the one who has faith in Jesus .
45003027	Where then is our boasting ? It is excluded . On what law ? On the law of works ? No , but on the law of faith .
45003028	For we hold that a man is justified by faith apart from works of the law .
45003029	Or is God the God of Jews only ? Is he not the God of Gentiles also ? Yes , of Gentiles also ,
45003030	since there is one God , who will justify the circumcised by faith and the uncircumcised through their faith .
45003031	Do we then nullify the law by this faith ? Certainly not ! On the contrary , we uphold the law .
45004001	What then shall we say that Abraham , our forefather according to the flesh , has found ?
45004002	For if Abraham was justified by works , he has something to boast about , but not before God .
45004003	For what does the scripture say ? » Abraham believed God , and it was reckoned to him as righteousness . «
45004004	Now to him who works , his wages are not reckoned as a gift but as his due .
45004005	And to one who does not work but trusts him who justifies the ungodly , his faith is reckoned as righteousness .
45004006	So also David describes the blessedness of the man to whom God reckons righteousness apart from works :
45004007	
45004008	
45004009	Is this blessedness only upon the circumcised , or also upon the uncircumcised ? For we say that faith was reckoned to Abraham as righteousness .
45004010	How then was it reckoned to him ? Was it after he had been circumcised , or before ? It was not after , but before he was circumcised .
45004011	And he received the sign of circumcision , a seal of the righteousness which he had by faith while he was still uncircumcised , that he might be the father of all who believe but have not been circumcised , in order that righteousness might be reckoned to them .
45004012	And he is also the father of the circumcised who are not only circumcised but who also walk in the footsteps of the faith which our father Abraham had before he was circumcised .
45004013	The promise to Abraham and his descendants , that he would be heir of the world , was not through the law but through the righteousness of faith .
45004014	For if those who are of the law are to be the heirs , faith has no value and the promise is void ,
45004015	because the law brings wrath , for where there is no law there is no transgression .
45004016	Therefore , the promise comes by faith , so that it may be by grace and may be guaranteed to all his descendants — not only to those who are of the law but also to those who are of the faith of Abraham , for he is the father of us all
45004017	( as it is written , » I have made you the father of many nations « ) in the presence of the God in whom he believed , who gives life to the dead and calls things that do not exist as though they did .
45004018	In hope , he believed against hope , so that he became the father of many nations ; as he had been told , » So shall your descendants be . «
45004019	And he did not weaken in faith when he considered his own body , which was as good as dead since he was about a hundred years old , or when he considered the barrenness of Sarah's womb .
45004020	He did not waver at the promise of God through unbelief , but was strengthened in his faith and gave glory to God ,
45004021	being fully convinced that God was able to do what he had promised .
45004022	That is why it was » reckoned to him as righteousness . «
45004023	But the words , » it was reckoned to him , « were written not for his sake alone ,
45004024	but for us also . It will be reckoned to us who believe in him who raised from the dead Jesus our Lord ,
45004025	who was delivered to death for our sins and was raised for our justification .
45005001	Therefore , since we have been justified by faith , we have peace with God through our Lord Jesus Christ ,
45005002	through whom we have obtained access by faith into this grace in which we stand , and we rejoice in our hope of the glory of God .
45005003	And not only that , but we rejoice in our sufferings , knowing that suffering produces perseverance ;
45005004	and perseverance , character ; and character , hope .
45005005	And hope does not disappoint us , because God has poured out his love into our hearts by the Holy Spirit who has been given to us .
45005006	When we were still weak , at the right time Christ died for the ungodly .
45005007	Why , one will hardly die for a righteous man — though perhaps for a good man one will dare even to die .
45005008	But God demonstrates his own love for us , in that while we were still sinners Christ died for us .
45005009	Since , therefore , we have now been justified by his blood , much more shall we be saved through him from the wrath of God .
45005010	For if , when we were enemies , we were reconciled to God through the death of his Son , much more , having been reconciled , shall we be saved by his life .
45005011	Not only so , but we also rejoice in God through our Lord Jesus Christ , through whom we have now received our reconciliation .
45005012	Therefore , just as sin entered the world through one man , and death through sin , so death spread to all men , because all men sinned .
45005013	For sin was in the world before the law was given , but sin is not counted when there is no law .
45005014	Nevertheless death reigned from Adam to Moses , even over those whose sins were not like the transgression of Adam , who was a type of the one who was to come .
45005015	But the free gift is not like the trespass . For if by the one man's trespass many died , much more the grace of God and the gift by the grace of the one man , Jesus Christ , abounded to many .
45005016	And the free gift is not like the effect of that one man's sin . For the judgment following one trespass brought condemnation , but the gift following many trespasses brings justification .
45005017	For if , by the one man's trespass , death reigned through that one man , much more will those who receive the abundance of grace and of the gift of righteousness reign in life through the one man Jesus Christ . )
45005018	So then , as one man's trespass led to condemnation for all men , so one man’s act of righteousness leads to justification and life for all men .
45005019	For just as through the disobedience of the one man the many were made sinners , so also through the obedience of the one man the many will be made righteous .
45005020	Law came in , that the trespass might increase . But where sin increased , grace abounded all the more ,
45005021	so that , as sin reigned in death , grace also might reign through righteousness to eternal life through Jesus Christ our Lord .
45006001	What shall we say then ? Shall we continue in sin that grace may abound ?
45006002	Certainly not ! How can we who died to sin live any longer in it ?
45006003	Or do you not know that all of us who were baptized into Christ Jesus were baptized into his death ?
45006004	We were buried therefore with him through baptism into death , so that just as Christ was raised from the dead by the glory of the Father , we too might walk in newness of life .
45006005	For if we have been united with him in a death like his , we shall certainly also be united with him in a resurrection like his .
45006006	We know that our old self was crucified with him so that the body of sin might be done away with , that we should no longer be slaves to sin .
45006007	For he who has died has been freed from sin .
45006008	Now if we died with Christ , we believe that we shall also live with him .
45006009	For we know that Christ , being raised from the dead , will never die again ; death no longer has dominion over him .
45006010	The death he died , he died to sin once for all ; but the life he lives , he lives to God .
45006011	So you also , consider yourselves dead to sin but alive to God in Christ Jesus .
45006012	Therefore do not let sin reign in your mortal body , that you obey its passions .
45006013	Do not yield your members to sin as instruments of wickedness , but yield yourselves to God as men who have been brought from death to life , and your members to God as instruments of righteousness .
45006014	For sin shall not have dominion over you , since you are not under law but under grace .
45006015	What then ? Shall we sin because we are not under law but under grace ? Certainly not !
45006016	Do you not know that if you yield yourselves to any one to obey as slaves , you are slaves of the one whom you obey , whether of sin , which leads to death , or of obedience , which leads to righteousness ?
45006017	But thanks be to God , that you who were once slaves of sin have become obedient from the heart to the standard of teaching to which you were committed ,
45006018	and , having been set free from sin , you have become slaves of righteousness .
45006019	I am speaking in human terms , because of the weakness of your flesh . For just as you once yielded your members to impurity and to greater and greater iniquity , so now yield your members to righteousness for holiness .
45006020	When you were slaves of sin , you were free in regard to righteousness .
45006021	But then what return did you get from the things of which you are now ashamed ? The end of those things is death .
45006022	But now that you have been set free from sin and have become slaves of God , the return you get is holiness and its end , eternal life .
45006023	For the wages of sin is death , but the free gift of God is eternal life in Christ Jesus our Lord .
45007001	Do you not know , brethren — for I am speaking to those who know the law — that the law has authority over a man only as long as he lives ?
45007002	For a married woman is bound by law to her husband as long as he lives , but if her husband dies she is released from the law of her husband .
45007003	So then , she will be called an adulteress if she lives with another man while her husband is alive . But if her husband dies , she is free from that law , and though she marries another man , she is not an adulteress .
45007004	Likewise , my brethren , you have died to the law through the body of Christ , so that you may belong to another , to him who was raised from the dead , in order that we may bear fruit to God .
45007005	While we were living in the flesh , our sinful passions , aroused by the law , were at work in our members to bear fruit for death .
45007006	But now , by dying to what once held us , we have been released from the law so that we serve in the new way of the Spirit , and not in the old way of the written code .
45007007	What shall we say , then ? Is the law sin ? Certainly not ! Indeed , I would not have known what sin was except through the law . For I would not have known what coveting really was if the law had not said , » You shall not covet . «
45007008	But sin , finding opportunity by the commandment , produced in me all kinds of covetous desire . For apart from the law sin lies dead .
45007009	I was once alive apart from the law , but when the commandment came , sin sprang to life and I died .
45007010	The very commandment which was to bring life I found to be death to me .
45007011	For sin , finding opportunity in the commandment , deceived me , and by it killed me .
45007012	So the law is holy , and the commandment is holy and just and good .
45007013	Did that which is good , then , become death to me ? Certainly not ! But it was sin , working death in me through what is good , in order that sin might be recognized as sin , so that through the commandment sin might become sinful beyond measure .
45007014	We know that the law is spiritual ; but I am carnal , sold under sin .
45007015	I do not understand what I do . For I do not do what I want to do , but I do what I hate .
45007016	Now if I do what I do not want to do , I agree that the law is good .
45007017	So then , it is no longer I who do it , but sin that dwells within me .
45007018	For I know that nothing good dwells within me , that is , in my flesh . I can will to do what is good , but I cannot do it .
45007019	For I do not do the good I want to do ; but the evil I do not want to do is what I do .
45007020	Now if I do what I do not want to do , it is no longer I who do it , but sin that dwells within me .
45007021	So I find it to be a law that when I want to do good , evil is present with me .
45007022	For I delight in the law of God , in my inner being ,
45007023	but I see in my members another law , at war against the law of my mind and making me captive to the law of sin which dwells in my members .
45007024	Wretched man that I am ! Who will deliver me from this body of death ?
45007025	Thanks be to God — through Jesus Christ our Lord ! So then , I of myself serve the law of God with my mind , but with my flesh I serve the law of sin .
45008001	There is therefore now no condemnation for those who are in Christ Jesus .
45008002	For the law of the Spirit of life in Christ Jesus has set me free from the law of sin and death .
45008003	For what the law could not do , in that it was weakened through the flesh , God did by sending his own Son in the likeness of sinful flesh , and for sin : he condemned sin in the flesh ,
45008004	in order that the righteous requirement of the law might be fulfilled in us , who do not walk according to the flesh but according to the Spirit .
45008005	For those who live according to the flesh set their minds on the things of the flesh , but those who live according to the Spirit set their minds on the things of the Spirit .
45008006	To set the mind on the flesh is death , but to set the mind on the Spirit is life and peace .
45008007	For the mind that is set on the flesh is hostile to God ; it does not submit to God's law , nor can it do so ;
45008008	and those who are in the flesh cannot please God .
45008009	But you are not in the flesh , you are in the Spirit , if in fact the Spirit of God dwells in you . And if anyone does not have the Spirit of Christ he does not belong to him .
45008010	But if Christ is in you , although your body is dead because of sin , your spirit is alive because of righteousness .
45008011	If the Spirit of him who raised Jesus from the dead dwells in you , he who raised Christ from the dead will give life to your mortal bodies also through his Spirit who dwells in you .
45008012	Therefore , brethren , we are debtors — not to the flesh , to live according to the flesh .
45008013	For if you live according to the flesh you will die ; but if by the Spirit you put to death the deeds of the body , you will live .
45008014	For all who are led by the Spirit of God are sons of God .
45008015	For you did not receive the spirit of bondage again to fear , but you received the Spirit of sonship by whom we cry out , » Abba , Father . «
45008016	The Spirit himself bears witness with our spirit that we are children of God ,
45008017	and if children , then heirs — heirs of God and fellow heirs with Christ , if indeed we suffer with him , in order that we may also be glorified with him .
45008018	I consider that the sufferings of this present time are not worth comparing with the glory that is to be revealed in us .
45008019	For the creation waits with eager expectation for the revealing of the sons of God .
45008020	For the creation was subjected to futility , not of its own will , but by the will of him who subjected it in hope ;
45008021	because the creation itself will be set free from its bondage to decay and obtain the glorious liberty of the children of God .
45008022	We know that the whole creation has been groaning in birth pangs together until now .
45008023	And not only the creation , but we ourselves , who have the firstfruits of the Spirit , groan inwardly as we wait eagerly for adoption as sons , the redemption of our bodies .
45008024	For in this hope we were saved . But hope that is seen is not hope . For who hopes for what he sees ?
45008025	But if we hope for what we do not see , we wait for it with patience .
45008026	Likewise the Spirit helps us in our weakness ; for we do not know what to pray for as we ought , but the Spirit himself intercedes for us with groans that words cannot express .
45008027	And he who searches the hearts of men knows what is the mind of the Spirit , because the Spirit intercedes for the saints according to the will of God .
45008028	And we know that in all things God works for the good of those who love him , who are called according to his purpose .
45008029	For those whom he foreknew he also predestined to be conformed to the image of his Son , that he might be the firstborn among many brethren .
45008030	And those whom he predestined , he also called ; those whom he called , he also justified ; and those whom he justified , he also glorified .
45008031	What then shall we say to this ? If God is for us , who can be against us ?
45008032	He who did not spare his own Son , but gave him up for us all , how will he not also give us all things with him ?
45008033	Who shall bring any charge against God's elect ? It is God who justifies .
45008034	Who is he who condemns ? It is Christ Jesus , who died , yes , who was raised from the dead , who is at the right hand of God , who is also interceding for us .
45008035	Who shall separate us from the love of Christ ? Shall tribulation , or distress , or persecution , or famine , or nakedness , or peril , or sword ?
45008036	As it is written : » For your sake we are being killed all the day long ; we are regarded as sheep to be slaughtered . «
45008037	No , in all these things we are more than conquerors through him who loved us .
45008038	For I am persuaded that neither death nor life , nor angels nor principalities , nor things present nor things to come , nor powers ,
45008039	nor height nor depth , nor anything else in all creation , will be able to separate us from the love of God which is in Christ Jesus our Lord .
45009001	I am speaking the truth in Christ , I am not lying ; my conscience bears me witness in the Holy Spirit ,
45009002	that I have great sorrow and unceasing anguish in my heart .
45009003	For I could wish that I myself were accursed and cut off from Christ for the sake of my brethren , my kinsmen according to the flesh .
45009004	They are Israelites , and to them belong the adoption , the glory , the covenants , the giving of the law , the worship , and the promises .
45009005	Of them are the patriarchs , and from them , according to the flesh , is the Christ , who is God over all , forever blessed . Amen .
45009006	But it is not as though the word of God had failed . For not all who are descended from Israel are Israel ,
45009007	nor are they all children of Abraham because they are his descendants ; but , » Through Isaac shall your descendants be named . «
45009008	In other words , it is not the children of the flesh who are the children of God , but the children of the promise are reckoned as descendants .
45009009	For this is what the promise said : » About this time I will return and Sarah shall have a son . «
45009010	And not only so , but also when Rebecca had conceived children by one man , our father Isaac ,
45009011	though the twins were not yet born and had done nothing either good or bad , in order that God's purpose of election might stand , not because of works but because of his call ,
45009012	she was told , » The older will serve the younger . «
45009013	As it is written , » Jacob I loved , but Esau I hated . «
45009014	What shall we say then ? Is there injustice with God ? Certainly not !
45009015	For he says to Moses , » I will have mercy on whom I have mercy , and I will have compassion on whom I have compassion . «
45009016	So it depends not upon man's will or exertion , but upon God's mercy .
45009017	For the scripture says to Pharaoh , » I have raised you up for this very purpose , that I may show my power in you , and that my name may be proclaimed in all the earth . «
45009018	Therefore he has mercy on whom he wills , and he hardens the heart of whom he wills .
45009019	You will say to me then , » Why does he still find fault ? For who can resist his will ? «
45009020	But who are you , O man , to answer back to God ? Will what is formed say to him who formed it , » Why have you made me like this ? «
